<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_and_funeral">Death and funeral</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=William_Henry_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Death and funeral">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Death_of_Harrison,_April_4_A.D._1841.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Death_of_Harrison%2C_April_4_A.D._1841.jpg/220px-Death_of_Harrison%2C_April_4_A.D._1841.jpg" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Death_of_Harrison%2C_April_4_A.D._1841.jpg/330px-Death_of_Harrison%2C_April_4_A.D._1841.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Death_of_Harrison%2C_April_4_A.D._1841.jpg/440px-Death_of_Harrison%2C_April_4_A.D._1841.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Death_of_Harrison,_April_4_A.D._1841.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Death of Harrison, April 4, 1841</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On March 26, Harrison became ill with a <a href="/wiki/Common_cold" title="Common cold">cold</a>. According to the prevailing medical misconception of that time, his illness was believed to be directly caused by the bad weather at his inauguration; however, Harrison's illness did not arise until more than three weeks after the event.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECleaves1939152_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECleaves1939152-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The cold worsened, rapidly turning to <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pleurisy" title="Pleurisy">pleurisy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECleaves1939152_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECleaves1939152-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> He sought to rest in the White House, but could not find a quiet room because of the steady crowd of office seekers. His extremely busy social schedule made any rest time scarce.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-64"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison's doctors tried cures, applying <a href="/wiki/Opium" title="Opium">opium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castor_oil" title="Castor oil">castor oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeches" title="Leeches" class="mw-redirect">leeches</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rauwolfia_serpentina" title="Rauwolfia serpentina" class="mw-redirect">Virginia snakeweed</a>, but the treatments only made Harrison worse, and he became delirious. He died nine days after becoming ill,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECleaves1939160_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECleaves1939160-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> at 12:30&#160;am on April 4, 1841. Harrison's doctor, Thomas Miller, diagnosed Harrison's <a href="/wiki/Cause_of_death" title="Cause of death">cause of death</a> as "pneumonia of the lower lobe of the right lung", but a 2014 medical analysis concluded that he instead died of <a href="/wiki/Enteric_fever" title="Enteric fever" class="mw-redirect">enteric fever</a>. The authors base their findings on the president's symptoms and the close proximity of the White House to a dumping ground for sewage and human waste.<sup id="cite_ref-What_Really_Killed_William_Henry_Harrison.3F_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-What_Really_Killed_William_Henry_Harrison.3F-78"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He was the first United States president to die in office. His last words were to his doctor, but assumed to be directed at John Tyler, "Sir, I wish you to understand the true principles of the government. I wish them carried out. I ask nothing more." Harrison served the shortest term of any American president: March 4&#160;– April 4, 1841, 30 days, 12 hours, and 30 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-dyingstmt_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dyingstmt-80"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Diamond_1976_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diamond_1976-81"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison's funeral took place in the <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Chapel_(Cincinnati)" title="Wesley Chapel (Cincinnati)">Wesley Chapel</a> in Cincinnati, Ohio, on April 7, 1841.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> His original interment was in the public vault of the <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Cemetery" title="Congressional Cemetery">Congressional Cemetery</a> in Washington, D.C. He was later buried in <a href="/wiki/North_Bend,_Ohio" title="North Bend, Ohio">North Bend, Ohio</a>. The <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Harrison_Tomb_State_Memorial" title="William Henry Harrison Tomb State Memorial">William Henry Harrison Tomb State Memorial</a> was erected in his honor.<sup id="cite_ref-ohiohistory_tomb_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiohistory_tomb-83"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_of_death">Impact of death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=William_Henry_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Impact of death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cincinnati-harrison-statue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cincinnati-harrison-statue.jpg/220px-Cincinnati-harrison-statue.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cincinnati-harrison-statue.jpg/330px-Cincinnati-harrison-statue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cincinnati-harrison-statue.jpg/440px-Cincinnati-harrison-statue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cincinnati-harrison-statue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue of Harrison <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_statue" title="Equestrian statue">on horseback</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati,_Ohio" title="Cincinnati, Ohio" class="mw-redirect">Cincinnati, Ohio</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Henry_Harrison_Memorial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/William_Henry_Harrison_Memorial.jpg/220px-William_Henry_Harrison_Memorial.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/William_Henry_Harrison_Memorial.jpg/330px-William_Henry_Harrison_Memorial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/William_Henry_Harrison_Memorial.jpg/440px-William_Henry_Harrison_Memorial.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="616" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Henry_Harrison_Memorial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The William Henry Harrison Memorial in North Bend, Ohio</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Harrison's death was a disappointment to <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">Whigs</a>, who hoped to pass a revenue tariff and enact measures to support Henry Clay's American system. <a href="/wiki/John_Tyler" title="John Tyler">John Tyler</a>, Harrison's successor and a former Democrat, abandoned the Whig agenda, effectively cutting himself off from the party.<sup id="cite_ref-tyler_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tyler-84"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Due to the death of Harrison, three Presidents served within a single calendar year (<a href="/wiki/Martin_Van_Buren" title="Martin Van Buren">Martin Van Buren</a>, Harrison, Tyler). This has happened on only one other occasion, 40 years later in 1881, when <a href="/wiki/Rutherford_B._Hayes" title="Rutherford B. Hayes">Rutherford B. Hayes</a> was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/James_A._Garfield" title="James A. Garfield">James A. Garfield</a>, who was assassinated later in that year. With the death of Garfield, <a href="/wiki/Chester_A._Arthur" title="Chester A. Arthur">Chester A. Arthur</a> stepped into the presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-americanhistory.about.com_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-americanhistory.about.com-85"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison's death revealed the flaws in the constitution's clauses on presidential succession.<sup id="cite_ref-art2_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art2-86"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Article_Two_of_the_United_States_Constitution#Clause_6:_Vacancy_and_disability" title="Article Two of the United States Constitution">Article II of the Constitution</a> states, "In case of the removal of the President from office, or of his death, resignation, or inability to discharge the powers and duties of the said office, the same shall devolve on the Vice President&#160;... and [the Vice President] shall act accordingly, until the disability be removed, or a President shall be elected". Scholars at the time disagreed whether the vice president would become president or merely acting President. The Constitution did not stipulate whether the Vice President could serve the remainder of the President's term, until the next election, or if emergency elections should be held.</p>
<p>Harrison's cabinet insisted that Tyler was "Vice President acting as President". After the cabinet consulted with the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Chief Justice of the Supreme Court of the United States" class="mw-redirect">Chief Justice</a> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taney" title="Roger Taney" class="mw-redirect">Roger Taney</a>, they decided that if Tyler took the presidential <a href="/wiki/Oath_of_Office" title="Oath of Office" class="mw-redirect">Oath of Office</a>, he would assume the office of President. Tyler obliged and was sworn in on April 6. In May, Congress convened. After a short period of debate in both houses, it passed a resolution that confirmed Tyler in the presidency for the remainder of Harrison's term. Once established, this precedent of presidential succession remained in effect until the <a href="/wiki/Twenty-fifth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Twenty-fifth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Twenty-fifth Amendment</a> was ratified in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-tyler_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tyler-84"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2admend_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2admend-87"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the assassination of John F. Kennedy and the succession of Lyndon B. Johnson to the presidency in 1963, the Twenty-fifth Amendment dealt with the finer points of succession. It defined in what situations the Vice President was acting President, and in what situation the Vice President could become President.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=William_Henry_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_William_Henry_Harrison_at_the_Indianapolis_Sailor_and_Soldier_Monument,_Indianapolis,_Indiana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Statue_of_William_Henry_Harrison_at_the_Indianapolis_Sailor_and_Soldier_Monument%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg/170px-Statue_of_William_Henry_Harrison_at_the_Indianapolis_Sailor_and_Soldier_Monument%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg" width="170" height="295" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Statue_of_William_Henry_Harrison_at_the_Indianapolis_Sailor_and_Soldier_Monument%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg/255px-Statue_of_William_Henry_Harrison_at_the_Indianapolis_Sailor_and_Soldier_Monument%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Statue_of_William_Henry_Harrison_at_the_Indianapolis_Sailor_and_Soldier_Monument%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg/340px-Statue_of_William_Henry_Harrison_at_the_Indianapolis_Sailor_and_Soldier_Monument%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1674" data-file-height="2909" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_William_Henry_Harrison_at_the_Indianapolis_Sailor_and_Soldier_Monument,_Indianapolis,_Indiana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue of Harrison at the <a href="/wiki/Soldiers%27_and_Sailors%27_Monument_(Indianapolis)" title="Soldiers' and Sailors' Monument (Indianapolis)">Soldiers' and Sailors' Monument</a> in Indianapolis</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tecumseh_in_Lafayette_IN.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Tecumseh_in_Lafayette_IN.jpg/170px-Tecumseh_in_Lafayette_IN.jpg" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Tecumseh_in_Lafayette_IN.jpg/255px-Tecumseh_in_Lafayette_IN.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Tecumseh_in_Lafayette_IN.jpg/340px-Tecumseh_in_Lafayette_IN.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1110" data-file-height="833" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tecumseh_in_Lafayette_IN.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Harrison (on left) at <a href="/wiki/Tippecanoe_County_Courthouse" title="Tippecanoe County Courthouse">Tippecanoe County Courthouse</a>, Lafayette, Indiana</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Harrison was the first sitting President to have his photograph taken, on Inauguration Day in 1841. Photographs exist of <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson" title="Andrew Jackson">Andrew Jackson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Martin_van_Buren" title="Martin van Buren" class="mw-redirect">Martin van Buren</a>, but those images were all taken after these men had ceased to be President. The Harrison image was also the first of these photographs to be taken. The original <a href="/wiki/Daguerreotype" title="Daguerreotype">daguerreotype</a>, made in Washington on his Inauguration Day, has been lost—although at least one early photographic copy exists in the archives of the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">Metropolitan Museum of Art</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-metmuseum_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metmuseum-88"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison's chief presidential legacy lies in his campaigning methods, which laid the foundation for the modern presidential campaign tactics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen2007100_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen2007100-89"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison died nearly penniless. Congress voted to give his wife a Presidential <a href="/wiki/Widow%27s_pension" title="Widow's pension">widow's pension</a>, a payment of $25,000,<sup id="cite_ref-Damon_1974-06_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Damon_1974-06-90"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> one year of Harrison's salary. This is equivalent to $571,532 today. She also received the right to mail letters free of charge.<sup id="cite_ref-firstladyorg_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstladyorg-91"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison's son <a href="/wiki/John_Scott_Harrison" title="John Scott Harrison">John Scott Harrison</a> served in the U.S. House of Representatives from Ohio between 1853 and 1857.<sup id="cite_ref-bioguide.congress_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bioguide.congress-92"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison's grandson, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison" title="Benjamin Harrison">Benjamin Harrison</a> of Indiana, was the 23rd president, from 1889 to 1893, making them the only grandparent–grandchild pair of Presidents.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun200543.E2.80.9349_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun200543.E2.80.9349-93"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Numerous places were named after Harrison:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harrison,_Michigan" title="Harrison, Michigan">Harrison, Michigan</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harrison,_New_Jersey" title="Harrison, New Jersey">Harrison, New Jersey</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harrison,_Ohio" title="Harrison, Ohio">Harrison, Ohio</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harrison,_Tennessee" title="Harrison, Tennessee">Harrison, Tennessee</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harrison_County,_Indiana" title="Harrison County, Indiana">Harrison County, Indiana</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harrison_County,_Mississippi" title="Harrison County, Mississippi">Harrison County, Mississippi</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harrison_County,_Iowa" title="Harrison County, Iowa">Harrison County, Iowa</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harrison_County,_Ohio" title="Harrison County, Ohio">Harrison County, Ohio</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Three schools were named William Henry Harrison High School (in <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Harrison_High_School_(Evansville,_Indiana)" title="William Henry Harrison High School (Evansville, Indiana)">Evansville</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Harrison_High_School_(West_Lafayette,_Indiana)" title="William Henry Harrison High School (West Lafayette, Indiana)">West Lafayette</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harrison,_Ohio" title="Harrison, Ohio">Harrison, Ohio</a>) in his honor.<sup id="cite_ref-WHHHS1_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHHHS1-94"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WHHHS2_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHHHS2-95"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WHHHS3_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHHHS3-96"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">Union Army</a> named a post near Cincinnati <a href="/wiki/Camp_Harrison" title="Camp Harrison">Camp Harrison</a>.,<sup id="cite_ref-ohiohistorycentral_Camp_Harrison_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiohistorycentral_Camp_Harrison-97"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> and a military fort in <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a> was named for him.<sup id="cite_ref-FtHarrisonMT_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FtHarrisonMT-98"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> Because of his short service, no military vessel was named after him as President.</p>
<p>A statue of Harrison was erected on <a href="/wiki/Monument_Circle" title="Monument Circle" class="mw-redirect">Monument Circle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>. Additionally, Harrison is shown (on the left, facing the building) in a <a href="/wiki/Pediment" title="Pediment">pediment</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Tippecanoe_County_Courthouse" title="Tippecanoe County Courthouse">Tippecanoe County Courthouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lafayette,_Indiana" title="Lafayette, Indiana">Lafayette, Indiana</a>, 1882.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=William_Henry_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Explanatory_notes">Explanatory notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=William_Henry_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Explanatory notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Harrison served as President for 30 days, 12 hours and 32 minutes, but this was spread over 32 different calendar days; part of a day upon inauguration, 30 full days, then part of the day on which he died.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
